It calls `Request.request()` (line 1170) which constructs an HTTP request using `r.newHTTPRequest(ctx)` and executes it via `client.Do(req)` - either the configured http.Client or http.DefaultClient.\\n\\nThe HTTP request is POST to `/apis/apps/v1/namespaces/{namespace}/deployments` with the Deployment object as JSON/Protobuf in the request body.\\n\\n## Layer 2: API Server (kubernetes--v1.32.0)\\n\\nOn the server side, the HTTP request is routed to the appropriate handler:\\n\\n1. **Storage Provider**: `pkg/registry/apps/rest/storage_apps.go:StorageProvider.NewRESTStorage()` (line 38) - This is the factory that creates all REST storage handlers for the apps API group. It calls `deploymentstore.NewStorage(restOptionsGetter)` to create the Deployment storage handler.\\n\\n2. **Deployment Storage**: `pkg/registry/apps/deployment/storage/storage.go:NewREST()` (line 93) - This creates a `REST` struct that embeds `*genericregistry.Store`. The Store implements the `rest.Storage` interface and handles all CRUD operations. The REST storage is registered at the path \\\"deployments\\\" in the APIGroupInfo's VersionedResourcesStorageMap.\\n\\n3. **Create Handler**: `staging/src/k8s.io/apiserver/pkg/registry/generic/registry/store.go:Store.Create()` (line 446) - This is the entry point for the create operation. It delegates to the internal `Store.create()` method (line 477).\\n\\n4. **Validation and Preparation**: Within `Store.create()`, the request goes through several validation stages:\\n   - `rest.BeforeCreate()` calls the CreateStrategy's `PrepareForCreate()` method\\n   - The CreateStrategy is `pkg/registry/apps/deployment/strategy.go:deploymentStrategy` which implements PrepareForCreate() (line 77) to clear status and set generation=1\\n   - `Store.create()` then calls `createValidation()` for admission webhook validation\\n   - Finally calls `deploymentStrategy.Validate()` (line 86) for validation logic\\n\\n5. **Storage Abstraction**: At line 526 of `Store.create()`, the actual storage call is made: `e.Storage.Create(ctx, key, obj, out, ttl, dryrun.IsDryRun(options.DryRun))` where e.Storage is a DryRunnableStorage.\\n\\n6. **Dry-run Wrapper**: `staging/src/k8s.io/apiserver/pkg/registry/generic/registry/dryrun.go:DryRunnableStorage.Create()` (line 39) - If not a dry-run, it delegates to the underlying `Storage.Create()`. This Storage is the etcd3 storage backend.\\n\\n## Layer 3: Storage (etcd-io/etcd)\\n\\nFinally, the data is persisted to etcd:\\n\\n1. **etcd3 Store**: `staging/src/k8s.io/apiserver/pkg/storage/etcd3/store.go:store.Create()` (line 241) - This prepares the Deployment object for storage:\\n   - Encodes the object using the codec: `runtime.Encode(s.codec, obj)`\\n   - Applies transformation (encryption if enabled): `s.transformer.TransformToStorage(ctx, data, ...)`\\n   - Generates an etcd key from the namespace and name\\n   - Obtains a lease if a TTL is specified\\n   - Makes the actual etcd call: `s.client.Kubernetes.OptimisticPut(ctx, preparedKey, newData, 0, kubernetes.PutOptions{LeaseID: lease})`\\n\\n2. **etcd Client**: `etcd-io-etcd/client/v3/kubernetes/client.go:Client.OptimisticPut()` (line 83) - This is the high-level wrapper around the etcd client v3 that uses optimistic concurrency control. It constructs an etcd transaction:\\n   ```\\n   txn := k.KV.Txn(ctx).If(\\n       clientv3.Compare(clientv3.ModRevision(key), \\\"=\\\", expectedRevision),\\n   ).Then(\\n       clientv3.OpPut(key, string(value), clientv3.WithLease(opts.LeaseID)),\\n   )\\n   txnResp, err := txn.Commit()\\n   ```\\n   This uses the etcd clientv3 library to atomically create the key-value pair in etcd with the specified lease (TTL).\\n\\n## Summary\\n\\nThe complete call chain is:\\n1. **Client**: client-go's `gentype.Client.Create()` → `rest.RESTClient.Post()` → `rest.Request.Do()` → HTTP POST request\\n2. **Server**: HTTP handler routes to `apps/deployment.REST` → `Store.Create()` → validates with `deploymentStrategy` → calls `DryRunnableStorage.Create()`\\n3. **Storage**: `etcd3.store.Create()` → encodes/transforms data → `kubernetes.Client.OptimisticPut()` → etcd transaction with `clientv3.Txn().If().Then().Commit()`\\n\\nThe key design pattern is layered abstraction: the client library abstracts HTTP details, the API server abstracts REST operations and validation, and the storage layer abstracts etcd details while providing optimistic concurrency control.\"\n}\n","structuredPatch":[],"originalFile":null}}
